Where we ended up was The Stardust, who had opened the first Race and Sports parlor in a casino on the strip. We sat at some high narrow tables like all sports bars have, under a ring of TVs bigger than any I had ever imagined. Each of them had a horse race on it. 
	The waitress addressed me, but Patra interceded and conferred with her closely for a moment. She returned only minutes later with two baskets of crab legs, a pitcher of beer, three mugs and… a glass of water with lemon. You can guess which one was hers. But there were also four racing forms and pens. We distributed them, and the girls began reading the horses running.
	“Let’s pick,” Patra said, looking at her watch, “five races. The first two of the afternoon have run, so start on the fifth.”
	Racehorse names are crazy. Plus, the form encompassed several races that were all broadcast live on different screens, so it was complicated. But we all filled them out, herself included, and that alone was fun. The girls conferred on their choices so as to prevent overlap, and Patra soon collected our bets. The race onscreen was already getting our attention, even though it wasn’t ours. 
	The timing was well planned by her, though. It wasn’t long after we had started cracking crab legs and drinking beer that our first race was up, and we were all cheering our respective picks. We won six races over the course of the afternoon, with Baby Boss winning a whopping three of her five picks. In fact, she picked up the tab with her largesse, so everything paid for itself. The only thing cooler would have been actual horseraces, which mostly has never been a thing in the history of Vegas, it seems. I think that would be a huge draw.
	I was beginning to enjoy Black Upper Class Vegas. This was the sort of thing I never would have done with the girls on my own, and it brought to mind how uneventful things had grown of late. If life was about enjoyment and experiences, I had been too narrowly focused on the daily pleasures my lifestyle had provided, up to that point. Not really living, as such.
	So, we had taken a few tiny bumps. The beer more or less demanded it, once we had our fill of crab. When we were in the cab en route to the show, I pulled out my case and lined me and the girls up some proper blasts. Even that felt different. 
	For one thing, the relaxed nature of the day, and my lack of worry, made doing cocaine feel less stressful. We didn’t even get a strong sense of disapproval from Patra. She had somehow made us subtly aware that she didn’t care for it, and that she wished we would stop, but other than that, it wasn’t an issue. It’s really what helped lead us to quit eventually. One of the reasons, anyway.
	At the ticket office, where we looked amazing, I might add, I asked for four, and the vendor asked for my I.D. At first, he said, “$104.68”, but as I pulled out some cash, he stopped me as he consulted a list.
	“Hold on. Mr. Clarence Jackson. The tickets are comped, sir. Have a great evening.”
	He slid me an envelope, and we were off, only slightly stunned. At the gate, I opened the envelope to find four tickets, which I hadn’t considered before that moment. But he had updated the quantity after Player’s Ball to account for Patra. Not only that, behind the tickets were four backstage passes for afterwards, and a keycard.
	“Concourse A, forward and to your left, suite six,” the ticket taker was telling me. I was only half listening.
	Suite six?
	Damned if they weren’t box seats or whatever you call them. A complete little lounge with couches, theater chairs, a door only we could open. It was plushed out, and I didn’t know you could watch a concert like that. It was kind of bloodless, not being in a crowd of sweating, screaming people, but it felt nice all the same. It was made even more so by the fact that there were speakers and screens. We were getting board sound from the stage, not just the auditorium. One of the cameras was already set close-up on center stage, and I realized I would get a better view from that than was possible at any concert.
	The girls fixed us drinks, and Patra got herself sparkling water. In the same festive mood, she opted for a slice of lime instead of lemon. But when we sat down, the girls didn’t try to flank me anymore. Patra sat to my right, Morgan was on my left, and Angela was beside Patra. It was an arrangement that felt natural for everyone involved.
	I am not going to rehash the concert here. Rest assured, the man was at the pinnacle of his career. It pains me to this day to know that he would be a paraplegic a few years later, leading to his early demise. I have people in the industry today that have told me that it was no accident, furthermore. As evidence, they say, his band was placed some fifteen feet back behind him, according to the stage marks. 
Every bit of the industry is dirty like that. All industries. But I’m not going into that, either. Janice says this book is going to end up in Lord of the Rings territory if I don’t learn how to push the narrative along. I can write some Ken Burns-ass music documentary shit some other time, according to her.
	Fair enough.
	The show was top-notch, though. There’s something about seeing it in a huge arena like that which reframes the context of everything. It *felt* very Black Upper Class Vegas. It wasn’t music you expected to hear in that environment, but it was perfectly suited, at the same time. Now, it feels like it was the pinnacle of civilization. The world really went downhill after that. Not for me, but in general.
	We stayed where we were until the very end, and everyone had walked off the now darkened stage. But as Mayfield was saying goodnight to the crowd, the last thing he actually said was, “Don’t forget about me, brother.” It now seems poignant, but at the time, I knew he was talking to me, without calling me out by name. I prefer to think he was making a general statement to everyone, and that we haven’t forgotten about him. I sure haven’t.
	I had no real idea of how to get to backstage. And I’m a man, so that means I don’t ask for directions. But we headed down in the general direction, and managed to find our way close enough that we were soon redirected there.
	Backstage at a show like that is crazy. We’re talking about thirty stage musicians, opening act included, and figure four times that many backstage personnel to handle them, if not more. Now on a post-show high, drinking, partying. Half-dressed carousing had already kicked off. Not a face we saw showed an emotion less than exuberance.
	Until we hit the green room. Mayfield was a somber man, still in his stage gear, tie and collar now loosened and unbuttoned. He sat on a couch at the far end of the room, flanked by two of his three female back-up singers. They wore gold, glittery gowns that hugged their figures and extended to their ankles. It was an enticing combination, given their exceptional beauty. The third sat on a chair to one side, and he stood to greet us. 
	“I am damn glad you decided to make it.”
	“I told you. I couldn’t miss it.”
	“A man of your word, too. But we knew that, didn’t we?”
	The girls sat on the empty couch that was opposite him, but he stayed standing, and we walked off together, leaving the gaggle of women together as Morgan and Angela excitedly engaged the singers in conversation about the night’s performance.
	We chatted about various things as he fixed himself a drink and finished it. Then he said, “Look, I’m on schedule to fly home tonight. Mrs. Mayfield is dearly expecting me. Last show of the tour. So, I’ll cut to the point. What do you think about Jade?”
	“Jade?” I thought he was referring to a gemstone.
	“Mrs. Mayfield is adamant of the subject of strays. I can’t bring her home with me.”
	He looked back at the cluster of girls around the coffee table, and I realized he was talking about one of the singers. The Asian one.
	“She’s beautiful,” I said, honestly. “They all are.”
	“Yes, but only Jade is ‘mine’. I kinda brought her out of The Life. She really can sing. But now I have nothing for her until next tour. That’s after an album. Probably six months.”
	“Damn.”
	“So, do you think you can take care of her for me? She’s a little upset, even though she knew this day was coming, months ago.”
	“I… Uh… Sure.”
	I had to think quick on my feet on that one. I had no idea where he was going with that right up until he said it. Wow. Damn.
	His face brightened considerably with relief.
	“My man. I knew you were the right one.”
	With that, he led me back over to them. 
	“Jade, honey, Mr. Clarence and friends said they would be delighted to be in your company for the near future, while we make arrangements for a return tour.”
	She stood up, the smile leaving her face in an instant, to be replaced with indifference.
	“I’ll be back, baby…”
	But he got nothing more from her, so he kissed her on the cheek.
	“I want to go,” the tall, gangly black back-up singer sitting near Jade said.
	Curtis raised his eyebrow at her, and then turned to look at me. All I could do was nod.
	“Good. See you folks on the next one,” he said, and shook my hand on his way to the door of his dressing room.
	I just stood there in stunned silence. Patra, naturally, saved the day.
	“You girls hungry?” she asked them.

Chapter 40 – Slumber Party

	This time, Patra took us all to an anonymous sort of greasy spoon, except the food was epic. That perfect stuff for when you come out of the bar kind of food, but really good. The two new girls, the singers, really put away a breakfast. We all got to know each other over coffee and messy sandwiches.
	Well, they got to know each other. I was now relegated to a background role, at least as far as the night was concerned. It was a relief to not have too much to deal with directly. Honestly, while I didn’t think I could handle Patra (who turned out to handle me, instead), I couldn’t have done anything like this without her. As it was, she smoothly facilitated the entire evening, down to sending the new girls’ luggage on ahead to the suite so we didn’t have to deal with it. Once or twice, she and Morgan made it a point to involve me in the conversation directly. But for the most part, it was girl’s night out.
	In fact, when we finally did call it a night and head back, she had already arranged for two more single beds to be installed in the piano room. I had done some thinking ahead in that regard, and that is not where my mind was ending up at all. Not where I was intending Jade to end up.
	But I hadn’t really worked out anything specific, and at the hotel, Patra wisely counseled me without directly saying anything about the situation, arranging for the new girls to bed down in the front room by themselves. She did include herself as a consolation prize, electing to spend the night with us for the first time. She and Morgan bookended me, and Angela clung to Patra, so everyone seemed happy.
	Later that night, I woke up to take a leak, and when I turned back around, I was startled to see her standing there in the dark. 
	“Come see,” she whispered, taking my hand. She led me to the front room in silence, where Jade and the other singer were sleeping cuddled together in a single bed.
	“Understand?”
	I kind of did. These weren’t average girls, despite the one’s background. I could see that from the start. If I had come in stepping all over their feelings, I doubt they would have stayed until morning. And Patra was helping to show me that they shouldn’t have in that case, furthermore. 
	She made good use of the kitchen that morning. Me and the girls awoke to the smell of coffee, and they soon joined her in prepping ingredients. Angie gently awoke the other two with cups and got their orders for omelets. Soon, we were all eating together, watching the mid-morning sun rise and talking quietly, while Patra nibbled on fruit.
	At one point, the black singer (“Mary,” she had told me. “All black female singers are named Mary.”) raised the question of an overall plan with Jade.
	“I don’t care, as long as I’m not on the road.”
	Mary seemed to be happy if Jade was happy. I still had no idea what I was going to do with any  of them. Thankfully, Patra intervened to smooth things over, as always.
	“The future is open-ended,” she told them. “But for now, we have all week here, with plenty to do.”
	With that, she pulled out a pile of brochures from the bar, and they all began to discuss the possibilities. When they were presently engaged, she took me into the bedroom and sat me by the phone. 
	“I’ll take both girls with me on a job tonight,” she began telling me. “Then I can put them to work some evenings while we’re here. Our burn rate is atrocious.”
	“What’s a burn rate?”
	“The speed with which we go through operating expenses.”
	She did have a point there, stilted language aside.
	“Then I’ll bring the other two in. By the end of the week, we’ll be back to a positive cash flow.”
	I just looked at her.
	“Now call de job, hus-bun. Someone mus’ work roun’ here…”
	With that, she rejoined the girls and finished planning their day. Our day.
	It was a real pain, back then, dealing with phone shit. The closest I could get to my boss was the field office, and rather than rely on a call back that may or may not ever happen, I elected to wait until he was rounded up, which took almost twenty minutes. Only for him to tell me I was fired as soon as I said I wouldn’t be back for a week, and then hang up.
	 Now, that was no thing, in and of itself. It wasn’t even the first time I had been fired. Twice I had busted x-rays doing plant work before I had perfected my technique. Getting another job wasn’t a problem in my occupation. It still took me aback. Everything else had changed, but I kind of felt that at least some things would stay the same. As it stood at that moment, I was entirely adrift. Untethered as a cosmonaut.
	Eventually, the girls agreed on a plan of attack for the day, guided by the ever-sly Patra. They spread out around the house in preparation, leaving me to mull the future over cooling coffee. The money situation was poor, that was for sure. Nothing had been budgeted like this, and that was before the two new girls or the extra week in town.
	I guess it’s an odd theme for a novel about pimping to keep harping on how bad I was at it, but I had never considered putting the girls to work in town while we were there. I couldn’t tell you what the protocols would be, but it would definitely require my close involvement. Which didn’t much feel like a vacation at that point. But I hadn’t even thought about it. Lucky for me, Patra had thought about everything, it seemed like.
	When we were all ready, which must have required 500 gallons of hot water from the hotel, all told, we squeezed into another cab, and I sorely missed the limo. 
	“I thought we would start small, and stay close, today,” Patra said after telling the driver where to go. “Skydiving.”
	It was a short trip, and we didn’t go to the airport. Instead, it was a place right on the strip, and we understood as soon as we got inside and saw the photos hanging in the lobby. After a moment’s consultation with her, I had rented a room for thirty minutes at a cost of four hundred dollars. The girls all rushed on ahead to get dressed, and she stayed behind with me. That was the first time I almost brought up the work situation with her and chickened out.
	 The place, Fly-Away, was wild, though. It had giant turbines in the floors covered with a grating. Wearing the suits they had fitted us with, we could hover over the fan indefinitely. With a little practice and guidance from Patra, who had clearly done it before, we were soon zooming around the room, narrowly missing collisions, and driving our beleaguered attendant insane.
	The kid did help us all join hands in a circle, though, and that turned out to be really cool. It actually felt like skydiving, at that moment. And I realized Patra had tricked us all into a team-building exercise.
	She finished our time off by showing us how to rise up to near the ceiling (which made me think of the Willie Wonka movie), and then curl into a ball, spreading back out before you hit the floor and stopping your fall. It only resulted in two bumped heads, one of them mine, which was hilarious, apparently. It was over before we knew it, and I understood that the half-hour rental was the right move. As Patra had pointed out, otherwise we would have only each gotten about 30 seconds of flight each for nearly half that much.
	For the second leg of the day, we took a shuttle, since it wasn’t far away, and a cab wasn’t exactly comfortable anymore. Shortly thereafter, we walked into a place called Wet and Wild. The lobby sold swimsuits, swim trunks, tote bags, suntan lotion, sunglasses, things like that. The girls all did the thing girls do on a shopping trip, and they spent an inordinate amount of time selecting suits, which involved multiple changes.
	This time, Patra paid for everything.
	“Business expense,” she said. 
	It was the first inkling I got that I had been mishandling my money terribly, and not just on this trip. It only took two words to open my eyes to the potential, there. Taxes mostly ate me alive at work, due to my bracket and filing status. I made a mental note to bring that up with her again later.
	Now, I kinda knew what this place was, but not really. The shuttle had let us out right in front of it, and I was too involved in escorting my entourage into the building to look up. So, I was unprepared when we stepped through the back doors and got in line for tickets.
	There was a waterslide something like seven stories tall, almost straight down. In fact, there were waterslides everywhere, each offering a different thrill. We rode them all, sometimes more than once. There was even a giant pool that made waves you could surf with bodyboards. It was late afternoon, and the sun had dipped behind the high-rises, when Patra suggested an early dinner and drinks, while we floated in the lazy river.
	It was the perfect suggestion. Our last hour was spent relaxing, full of food and drink, and I think we mostly dozed with smiles on our faces.
	Back at the hotel, another cramped cab ride later, and they all set about to showering again. It was a whirlwind of preparation that ended with Patra leaving with Morgan and Angela.
	“We’ll be back about ten, Daddy,” she said on the way out. “Have fun.”
	I went back to the bedroom to find both girls kneeling on the bed, half facing each other, my belt between them.
	“Good evening, sir…” Jade said.

Chapter 41 – Entourage

	It was an amazing week in Vegas, entirely facilitated by Patra. Jet skis at Lake Mead. Hiking. A helicopter ride to the Grand Canyon… Our days (and nights) were filled. Meanwhile, her first job with Morgan and Angela as apprentices netted me around six hundred dollars. I later found out that the portion she had turned over to me was a damn tip. She legitimately made two to three thousand dollars for a little more than an hour. And she never had sex with anyone for it, in any way.
	Not on the receiving end, at any rate.
	The way she explained it to me, she was paid as much for discretion and sympathy as anything. Her clients were rich, obviously, which translates into powerful. They paid her for the privilege of pretending to not be those things for a little while. They were all white, to hear her tell it, and the fact that she was a black female only enhanced the overall effect. Not only could she be trusted completely (blackmail was very much a thing in those circles), but she was understanding and non-judgmental. Except when her job required otherwise. Patra assured me that she was an excellent domme, and I had no doubt of her abilities, there.
	In fact, I had no doubt of her abilities in any area of life. All week, I watched her coordinate our days, schedule their nights, juggle finances, and she did it all with relative ease. One thing she wasn’t able to do was stop moving and doing. When she had gone through her Vegas clients, who regarded her appearance in town as some sort of holiday for them (I still can’t understand male submissives other than academically), she convinced a few from out of state to fly in at her request. Financial dominance, she called it. I had sort of thought she was kidding, at the time.
	All of those other things aside, the psychology never stopped. While I didn’t understand her clients, I did gain some level of knowledge about Patra herself. I think she was so smart that she liked things complicated. The more complicated the better. The way she coordinated the girls alone was masterful. Each night found me with a different combination of women. All except her, for the most part. I think she could have done without actual sex in her life entirely. How’s that for complicated?
	She spent part of her time with me filling me in on financial strategies. Everything she did seemed more criminal than my little small-time operation, and almost every bit of it was one hundred percent legal. Tax avoidance, she said, was a time-honored tradition. It was tax evasion that was illegal. In fact, the only actual crime she ever committed, technically, was in the select few clients she, uh, penetrated. For that reason alone, she charged an exorbitant amount, and wouldn’t do it for just anyone.
	Patra had not one, but two corporations in her name. One was a charity. It was a level of sophistication I had never dreamt of. Corporations were, like, Xerox, to me. Not some woman spanking rich white men. So, I received a thorough education that week. Her legitimate business profits sometimes got donated to her charity. Between the two, every aspect of her life was paid for in a way that generally reduced or eliminated her tax burden at the end of the year.
	“Pay yourself first,” she told me. No argument there. But the way she had things arranged, her income was never touched and instead went into, not savings, but long-term investments. Patra was a pimp with accountants. 
Yes, I considered Patra a pimp, more so than I was. I think those girls would have followed her anywhere. At least as long as I was in tow, and she manipulated me as thoroughly as anyone. The entire time I knew her, though, everything she did was benevolent. Beneficial, even. By the end of the week, I felt relatively comfortable in making moves in the same direction she was operating in. There was really no better time, because I had somehow blown about half of my accumulated savings by then.
All good things must come to an end, of course. The flight out went as smoothly as could be expected, due in large part to her leadership. I was a figurehead, in a sense. In another, she was my proxy. The relationship worked. Any doubts that I was a pimp when I had arrived in Vegas were erased upon my departure, with five gorgeous women who were clearly mine in tow. 
Nevermind that I had blown a large part of what had taken me years to earn. The flight was great for everyone else but me, however. The closer we got to home, the worse I felt. There was no glamour ahead. As Vegas receded in the distance, so did my confidence. Getting a new cover job wouldn’t be hard, and in theory, my income level would likely soon exceed anything I had ever made before. At the same time, something about it all didn’t feel right. I think it was the showgirls that did it to me, somehow. They were like taking exotic birds from the jungle and plopping them down in a parking lot.
Suddenly, the relatively luxurious apartment seemed small and seedy. My horizons had been expanded, but reality had yet to catch up. The only thing that distracted me from the situation even momentarily was that there was a package waiting for me when we got there. A package from Maxxy.
	I had gotten out her cipher book in anticipation of another involved letter, but in the box was just a note and a book, with no translation needed. I suspect she had outgrown her code, and I felt a little sadder knowing that. The note just said, “I stand corrected.”
	The book was a small paperback, “Farnham’s Freehold” by Robert Heinlein.
	I had no idea what she meant by that, and I didn’t understand for a week or so. Initially, I just put it aside while Patra and I reorganized. My girls got back to their regulars, aided by the twenty or so answering machine messages accumulated during our vacation. Patra pulled out her client book and started making a few calls. Soon enough, she was taking the new girls out with her. It’s a good thing, because they were not the type to streetwalk. One had, once upon a time, but those days were long gone.

He was an ex-military cat, as a lot of higher-ups in that industry are. He explained to me that he’d put me on if he could, but that he wouldn’t be in the states. If I got a passport, he said, he sure could use me in Germany, though. The pay was tremendous, and the unspoken part was that there was plenty of side money to be made on top of that. More than ever.
	When I explained the lamentable situation to Patra later that evening, she said, “You don’t have a passport?” Me and my two girls (I never really did accept the others as ‘mine’) were the only ones who didn’t. I called back old dude and accepted the offer. Patra went into overdrive. She really just did enjoy challenges and complicated situations. The things other people might have felt overwhelming were where she felt most at home, somehow. Patra took on both organizing the trip and hustling up cash for it. Some nights I was home alone during those next few weeks.
	Which was fine with me, as Maxxy was trying to communicate something to me. Some of my puzzlement was erased when I finally opened it, and saw a hand-written note from her. When I read it, I understood what “I stand corrected” meant.
	“A Heinlein book with black people!” she wrote. “It addresses race, and power! Awkwardly uses the n-word!”. Smiley face. Heart. “Maxxy” written in her mixed block and cursive handwriting, which would always stay somewhat child-like and sloppy. You’d never know she was a genius by the way she wrote.
	It provided a good escape from the invisible pressure I was feeling. The idea of moving overseas was beyond intimidating. And Germany? Everything I knew about the world, or thought I did, told me that was no place for me to be. Then again, your northern types said that to me about Texas, and I had thrived there. It really wasn’t his best work, his attempt to deal with racial issues aside. “Stranger in a Strange Land” would always be my favorite. I never understood why people said he was embarrassed by it in later years. 	
	I managed to keep most of my concerns to myself, and the girls were jubilant. The move was exactly what was needed to keep the group cohesive and moving forward. The Vegas girls were not going to stick around for long in the sticks. For one thing, Patra was introducing them to high-end clients on a nightly basis. It would be trivial for one or both of them to jump ship at any time, after that. They could get set up as a mistress somewhere, or elect to work solo, poaching a few clients. Life is kind of wide-open when you’re a young and beautiful woman, if you have a good head on your shoulders, and zero responsibility. 
	Once I got all my paperwork in order, which involved all the usual hiring stuff, plus the addition of a drug test, physical, a few shots (I didn’t think Malaria was a big concern in Germany…), plus providing my passport, three weeks had elapsed. Before I knew it, I was collecting my deposit on the rental, and we were donating everything we couldn’t bring with us.
	I did take the opportunity to call both Til and my mother. Til informed me that Maxxy had been accepted to college at age fifteen. In other news, she was fifteen. Where did the damn years go? When she got on the phone, she didn’t really want to talk about school. Instead, she quizzed me on the book and what I thought about it. It was really hard getting off of the phone with them, and I definitely shed a tear or two. My mother and aunt were encouraging, I suppose, but that ship had mostly sailed. I was glad they had gotten out of the ward and seemed to be doing well. Happy. What more can you hope for people in life?
	Pretty much a month to the day we had come back from Vegas, we were touching down in Europe. Tokio was international. Except I was still Clarence, inside and out.

Chapter 42 – Willkommen in Deutschland
I had two things going for me that allowed me to step foot on foreign soil for the first time ever. First and foremost was Patra. She handled the endless details of the trip in a way that neither I nor any of my girls could. Angela was pretty capable, but she wasn’t nearly as motivated or energetic as Patra was. The rest of them simply didn’t have it in them at all, for various reasons.
	The second was that it was, to me, basically just an extended, more involved version of getting a new job. The construction work was familiar, and universal. The only change in the process was the addition of a passport and a few shots. I’ll say right now, I didn’t trust shots then, and I trust them even less now, having learned a good deal more since I was young and stupid. Luckily, I haven’t had any ill effects.
	I needed something to ease me into this, because it wasn’t just Europe, but Germany. Everything in my limited knowledge and experience told me it was no place for a black man. Again, people also said that about Texas, and I had thrived there. Patra said I was entirely off base and misinformed, and as usual, she was right.
	“So long as you’re not disrupting the natives, you’ll be fine.”
	“Who are the natives?”
	She looked at me somewhat puzzled.
	“The Germans.”
	“Oh.”
	Patra explained to me that she had always been warmly received in Germany, despite their sordid history. Or, as she told it, perhaps because of it. She went on to tell me about Jesse Owens and the 1936 Berlin Olympics, in which the Nazis were of course involved, and where swastikas were heavily present…
	In a story reminiscent of Muhammed Ali and Vietnam, in which he famously said, “Ain’t no Vietnamese ever called me a nigger,” Owens said that he was more poorly treated by his own countrymen than any German. It has been said that Hitler snubbed the gold-medal winner who single-handedly destroyed the myth of “Aryan” superiority, but I’ve also read that he didn’t shake any American winner’s hand.
	Not that Hitler wasn’t a huge piece of shit, but all world leaders were, are, and forever will be. America kills us by the millions in various ways every year. They’ve just refined their techniques. In fact, I’ve come to believe we live in the 4th Reich today. But that’s too much to get into in this book. You should study who founded NASA and the NSA.
	Germany was pretty cool from the jump. If I thought Patra’s American clients loved her, the Germans were fanatical about her. She hadn’t been there in nearly two years, and a few of them met us at the airport, with a warm reception. Three men, one whom which brought his entire family, wife, kids, everything. It was all hugs and incomprehensible chatter. Of course Patra was fluent in German. What couldn’t she do?
	We were pre-checked into a luxury hotel, and once again, our luggage went off without us, as we were given the full tourist treatment, including a brief tour via taxi, leading to an authentic German dinner, complete with big steins of beer. It was almost like two separate groups at one big table, as she sat near the “natives” as they all spoke to each other in German, and me and the other girls just sort of ate and took it all in. Morgan and Angela were the most impressed. These poor girls had never been anywhere, just like me. It felt good to see their horizons expanded in such a grand manner. The other two had been around the world, but mostly only saw backstage, hotels, and mattresses.
	After a two-hour dinner and an irregular amount of beer, they said their goodbyes. As they were leaving, Patra said to one of them, “Krell?”, to which he replied, “Ja”, and handed her a packet. In the ride back to the hotel, I said, “What was that about?”
	“This?” she said, handing it to me. “A gift. I have to go out tonight, I thought it might keep you all entertained.”
	I didn’t open it in front of the girls, because I kind of knew. They didn’t ask about it, wisely, and at the hotel, I flushed it. Crazy, I know, but we had been off of the coke for about a month and half. I couldn’t see starting back up. It’s never a one-time thing. I’m pretty proud of myself for that. I mean, do you know what it’s like to fool around with four coked-up whores? No, of course you don’t. That’s why you read about it instead of writing about it. But, for the record, four non-coked-up whores are also pretty fun.
	 The next day I told Patra, and she never did that again. I had enough nervous energy as it was. Being out of the country did it, for one thing. But the other was just because I was hiring on to a new job. I think that always makes a lot of people nervous, no matter what. Probably because incomes are so vital to our survival. I felt that way even though I didn’t technically need a job at all, other than as a cover story and to account for the money I spent.
	It was a Liquified Natural Gas plant. If you don’t know how complicated something like that is, imagine walking around inside a computer motherboard. No, that’s not right. Imagine being inside a computer processor. It was a five-year project, and the ground was just being broken. I was already hired in, and didn’t actually have anything to worry about. But that didn’t stop me from worrying.
	Patra had the work lined up on her side, too. There was no shortage of money or interest in Germany. In fact, they were all busier than ever. The money started rolling in again, only about 25% of it was American currency. The rest was Marks, Francs, Pounds, Lira. It was complicated just keeping track of all the exchange rates. Once I had settled in at work (there was nothing for me to weld for months, which was sort of the plan), I took to sightseeing and traveling in my off time.
	I’d usually just take a girl or two with me. Sometimes I even went out alone, a few times for a whole weekend, even.
	Europe is a trip. It’s, I don’t know, the size of Texas. Changing countries is quicker and easier than traveling state to state in the U.S., by far. You can accidentally walk into another country, in fact. And that’s how little emphasis there was on borders, too. Other than major thoroughfares, there weren’t hardly ever any restrictions on where you could go. Unless you wanted to go to East Germany.
	No one wanted to go to East Germany. Aside from that, Europeans were pretty cool about everything. They were friendly all over, for the most part, and didn’t make me feel like a freakshow. Because, I gotta say, at that time, there weren’t a lot of black people over there. At least not in the parts of Germany I visited. Meeting some of them was wild, too. Because they didn’t think of themselves as black, but as Germans. Or as black Germans, I guess. But it was mostly secondary to them. It’s a stark contrast to how we are in the states.
	There were clubs, though, for sure. Most weekends, the girls wanted to go dancing and drinking. That wasn’t my sort of thing, of course, but I was obligated to attend as chaperone and security. Protecting my investments. The problem was, German women were pretty intensely interested in me, some of them, but I had a small army of loyal, jealous hoes. So I didn’t take the bait, for the most part. Several put themselves on offer to work for me, but the vibe just wasn’t right. If I had met one that had fit in and jibed with the other girls, I would have taken them up on it. But I never did. I did sleep with a few of them on the low, and they mostly enjoyed it more than I did. Go figure.

More to the point, Patra helped me incorporate in Connecticut, twice. One for profit, and one non-profit. That and the basic principles of money laundering went a long way. With the per diem paying my living expenses tax free, I was able to invest more or less my entire salary into the market. Stocks and bonds. The saving grace is that the government can’t track what you spend. If that ever changes, I think we’ll all be fucked.
	She taught me about high and low risk investments, something a pimp knows a little about. But the other thing I started putting money into was real estate. Because Patra was a real whiz in this area. Apparently before she became a domme, she had a realtor’s license. She was successful at that, too, naturally. But, she said, a bank had basically fucked her over for no reason, putting a hold on a major deposit, causing her to lose a big client and a bunch of money.
	She and I didn’t even have to talk about why. Sometimes bad shit happens to you just because you’re black. It’s not even worth discussing with white people because it just sounds like excuses or paranoia. If only you could spend some time in my shoes. Or Patra’s. So she renounced the straight world of banking and real estate, turned in her license and never looked back. Now she owned more land than she knew what to do with, and frequently flipped properties over the phone for outrageous profit. Patra said she owned a mountain in Appalachia, and I didn’t doubt her at all.
	The other thing I did at her behest was sign up with the same accounting firm she used. This was some counterintuitive shit that I wouldn’t have ever done on my own. Even with her urgings and explanations, I was extremely reluctant to turn over my finances to some outside agency. Matter of fact, it was the first and only time I really became suspicious of her and her intentions. Part of me was convinced it was a long-term hustle that was going to result in my account being drained and her ghosting me. 
What happened instead was that I got monthly reports on how my money was doing. I deposited a hundred percent of my income and per diem, because the government also doesn’t care if your finances make any sense, as long as they get theirs. Within three months of doing that, combined with the initial lump sum I had on account, the income from investments began to dwarf the cost of the accountants. Patra assured me that the real savings would come at tax time, and of course she was proven right there, too.
	So money was no longer a problem. In fact, we took to juicing the Germans for a lot more than the girls were pulling down in the states. Scarcity breeds value or something, I think the phrase is. They were rare, and beautiful, and in demand. There were some gorgeous black women in Germany, to be sure. But they weren’t hoes. And if they were, they weren’t my hoes.
	Morgan and Angela had really mastered the upsell. I’m sure it was as much stuff Patra had taught them as anything, but the money came to me, either way. The other two did okay. They fetched a fair price, but they really didn’t think of themselves as whores, and did pretty much the bare minimum. Ordinarily, that would have been a red flag. But I still had to eat at least sixty hours a week at work, and I wasn’t one to rock my own boat too hard, at that point.
	Patra’s contribution was our lodging and accommodations. The entire time I was there, I never paid rent, bills, anything. My primary expenses were food and fuel. Now, gas is some crazy stuff in Europe. They sell it in liters, not gallons, and a liter there costs what a gallon does here. That’s why they drive tiny cars in a lot of places. Not so much Germany, which naturally featured a lot of Mercedes for the upper class. But even then, post-gas crisis, it was the dawn of the Jetta and cars like that. Plus, you have never seen so many Volkswagen beetles in your life. 
	Patra taught me a lot of crazy stuff about Germany. I didn’t know Volkswagen was a Nazi brand. It literally means “The People’s Car” in German. The fact that the name didn’t change after WWII tells you a lot about America, and the world. But that’s just scratching the surface. Some of the stuff she told me led to my fascination with that era, after a time. It slowly became a subject of mild academic study for me. At this point, I honestly believe we live in the 4th Reich in America, at this point.
	That’s probably the most controversial statement in a book full of them, so allow me to explain. It’s a touchy subject, even today, and only my skin color keeps people from accusing me of being a Nazi myself when I talk about it. It’s not just the subject of polite discussion. After breaking it down for me one evening as she and I sipped warm beers while the girls frolicked (they were basically given a pass by me to do cocaine as long as it was free and didn’t interfere with my life – a major attraction of the nightclub lifestyle they favored), she recommended a life-changing, eye-opening book. It was the first of many academic tomes, but the most important of the bunch.
	I.G. Farben, she said, was a chemical plant. Something I well understood. Actually, though, it was a plant owned by an umbrella corporation of the same name. Umbrella corporation, or something like that. A joint venture of several corporations. The Germans really were hard-working and industrious, and that kinda worked against the rest of the world, I guess. Or the people who purported to run it.
	To hear Patra tell it, Germany was considered sort of a threat to what she called “global hegemony”. They were efficient and intelligent in their business and industry, and in the early 1900s, they were coming up hard compared to the rest of the world. They didn’t have much of anything by way of natural resources, so being industrious was the only way they could prosper as a people. They weren’t lazy, I’ll tell you that.
	On one hand, Farben researchers were the saviors of Germany industry because of their invention of what are called synthetic dyestuffs. Now this doesn’t sound like a big deal in the modern age. Everything is synthetic, it seems like. But back then, dyes were still derived from the natural world. Indigo, blue, essentially, for example was hella expensive, because it came primarily from the indigo plant. This natural approach was increasingly at odds with the demands of a growing population. And this applied to all dyes.
	Synthetic dyes were a big breakthrough, in other words. It’s one of the things that led to today’s notion that anything can just be synthesized in a laboratory. In a sense, the German attitude, decidedly non-naturalist, became the pervading mode of thought world-wide. 
	The flips side of all this otherwise seemingly unimportant discovery was that the rest of the world was concerned with Germany’s growing economic dominance. This led to World War I, which was literally started over some dumb shit. But that’s a part of the history books. What it actually achieved, however, was forcing the German government to put pressure on I.G. Farben to produce more synthetics. Namely gunpowder, gasoline, and rubber. War material. Materiel, Janice just said. Whatever.
	This is part of where it gets fascinating, to me. Gunpower was mostly nitrate, and all of its components were mined from the Earth. In those days, mostly places in South America. So it wasn’t too hard to cut the supply off. Awareness of their vulnerability is what led to the development of the synthetic gunpowder. Most people don’t know that almost everything in their lives today is derived from petroleum. That’s why I laugh at people who want to get rid of cars or whatever. 95% of civilization would die off in a year if we didn’t have oil. Almost anything today that isn’t wood, cotton, or an animal is a byproduct of oil. 
	They didn’t have a lot of luck with synthetic rubber back then, but obviously that was possible, and it exists in various forms today. What they did also develop, though, was synthetic gasoline. I can’t tell you what it was made from, but they did the damn thing, in the 30s, no less. But it wasn’t considered cost-effective.
	There’s no way it’s not cost effective now. We are definitely being lied to. Just like the notion that oil comes from dinosaurs or whatever crazy stuff they teach us in school. Oil comes from what is called an abiotic process deep inside the earth. It’s definitely renewable. Old wells that were capped off can be reopened a decade or two later, and are ready to be pumped again. The notion of scarcity is what’s artificial. In fact, one could make the argument that the defense industry hustle itself is just oil company shit. A huge part of the military budget is fuel.
	This effort Germany put into looking ahead prepared them for WWII. With even more perspective now, I daresay this was all contrived as well. It was a play for the global stage. Because did you know the British royal family are of German descent? That fascism was very popular in England until it became unfashionable with the rise of Hitler? Hitler, whom (I don’t say ‘whom’. – Tokio.) (Who does? – Janice.) I should remind you, was on the cover of Time Magazine as Man of the Year, once. Now they say it wasn’t a celebration of him, but of course it was.
	So, during WWII, the Farben plant drew more power than the city of Berlin itself. That’s staggering, if you know how big Berlin is. Naturally, a lot of the labor was derived from POWs. The camps you know as death camps were actually labor camps. Prisoners woke up at something like 4 am, marched ten miles to work at the plant for 12 hours, then marched back. If they fell out, they were useless. Killed.
	The operators of the plant eventually decided this wasn’t the best use of their labor pool, and built a new camp, which you would know as Auschwitz III, on site. 
	The kicker of all of this, which I assure you is just the tip of the iceberg where concerns the intrigue surrounding WWII, is this. Some of the primary members of Interessen-Gemeinschaft Farbenindustrie AG? Bayer, AGFA, BASF, and Kodak…
	The plant I was working at in Berlin was a BASF facility! I ate Bayer aspirin for headaches, and we all used Kodak film and cameras. What people consider good old American companies were literally part of the Nazi war machine. The company that became IBM and invented the entire computing industry did information technology out of New York for the Nazis during the war. Openly.
	Once you combine that knowledge with the fact that we brought something like 8,000 Nazi leaders and scientists to the U.S. after WWII, and they headed up the agencies that became NASA and the NSA (Which most people don’t even know exists. They are bigger than the CIA, and far less well-known...), then I submit to you that my premise, that we in the U.S. (if not the world) live under the 4th Reich as envisioned by Hitler, becomes irrefutable.
	It’s not a subject of casual conversation, and it’s not hard to see why. “What luck for rulers that men do not think.” – Adolf Fucking Hitler… (“Like the fascism/corporatism quote attributed to Mussolini, possibly apocryphal. But no less true, regardless.” – Janice.)
	Of course, my dumb ass was working hard and reading a lot when I wasn’t working. I got complacent. Two things happened almost simultaneously that snapped me out of it: the performers bounced on me out of the blue, going back on the road with Mayfield, who was clearly 10x the pimp I would ever be, without actually doing any pimping, and I got a phone call from a Ms. Maxine Jackson of Los Angeles, California.
